Current Commentary

Sir Otto Niemeyer's Visit to China

— Line

Sir Otto Niemeyer, the British government's chief economic advisor, set out for China on the tenth of this month, accompanied by Mr. Patchett of the British Treasury and Mr. Rogers, an expert from the Bank of England. He will pass through Tokyo, where he will stay for several days to discuss Far Eastern economic issues with Japanese government officials. As a result, various rumors have arisen. Some say that Niemeyer's visit is intended to reform China's currency system, bringing our country into the sterling area. Others say that Britain will propose to Japan a new alliance similar to the Anglo-Japanese Alliance of the past. Even if the British side has such intentions, it seems not easy to realize in the current situation. However, Niemeyer's visit carrying a plan for economic assistance to China, is what he has formally expressed and is also known to all of us.

There is no other way to assist China's economy today than investment. The purpose of the investment, let us put it aside for the moment. As for its form, it can only be in two ways: one is individual investment, and the other is joint investment. In order to consolidate its economic position in the Far East, Britain has long had the intention of investing in China alone. It is only because of numerous obstacles that it has not been agreed upon. A foreign dispatch盛傳盛傳盛傳盛傳盛傳盛傳盛傳盛傳a few months ago that London had another proposal for joint investment in China by Britain, the United States, France, and Japan. Niemeyer's visit to Japan is probably mainly for this mission.

It is still difficult to know whether Japan is willing to leave room for consultation on joint investment recently. However, not long ago, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs formally declared its opposition to this proposal. Judging from Japan's various measures toward China recently, it is clear that Japan is very determined to exclude the influence of foreign powers in the Far East. Japan's plans for individual investment in China are already in active progress. The Northeast is, of course, undeniable. After the North China issue came to an end, the so-called Xingfaxiang Bank and Xingzhong Company and other companies are being organized successively. The investigation and construction of railways and cotton fields are also prepared to be carried out on a large scale. Tatsuiro Funatsu, chairman of the Japan Textile Industry Association in China, also said in an interview that in ten years, Beijing and Tianjin will become the center of the Eastern textile industry. It is truly to be called looking down on everything.

We deeply know by comprehensively viewing today's situation that Britain advocates joint investment, while Japan advocates individual investment. Britain wants to provide general assistance to China, while Japan wants to start with the development of North China and proceed gradually. British investment advocates taking the procedure of negotiating with our government, while Japanese investment advocates taking the investment form of joint ventures between Chinese and Japanese private enterprises. With such conflicting opinions, if Niemeyer's visit to Japan really involves persuading Japan to join the consortium, can he achieve any success?

Niemeyer has already come to China. Whether this mission can be completed depends on the results of his visit to Japan. It can be clarified. Today, our country, internally, has its various industries in decline, rural areas bankrupt, and natural and man-made disasters succeeding each other. Externally, it is suffering from the double blow of Japan's continental policy and the US silver purchase policy. In terms of the current political and economic situation, it is no different from Germany after the war. Its urgent need for economic assistance from other countries is undeniable. If Niemeyer's visit can indeed promote the realization of investment in China, then whether it is individual or joint action, our country should carefully consider whether the investment conditions are limited to economic and technical plans without infringing on our sacred national sovereignty. On the other hand, whether the nature of the investment is based on China's overall financial and economic situation and has no meaning of disguised partition. This is a prerequisite for acceptance or not, and the whole country should pay close attention to it.

Generalissimo Chiang's Circular Telegram: Instructions for Flood Relief and Economic Construction Must Not Be Delayed

(Chengdu) Generalissimo Chiang sent a telegram on the 8th to the governments of various provinces and the people of all regions, outlining the initial key points for flood relief and the promotion of national economic construction. The full text is as follows: To the chairmen of the provincial governments and, through them, to all compatriots: This year, the rivers have overflowed, causing widespread flooding, affecting provinces in the Yangtze and Yellow River basins. Crops have been submerged, villages have been destroyed, and the loss of land and property is incalculable. The plight of our compatriots in the disaster areas, adrift and suffering, is particularly tragic. The severity of the disaster in Hubei, Henan, and Shandong provinces surpasses even that of the twentieth year of the Republic of China (1931). On the verge of exhaustion, they have once again suffered this calamity. How can my compatriots endure this fate? Regarding disaster relief and the resettlement of refugees, the entire nation should make active efforts. However, it is even more important to learn from past mistakes and prevent future disasters through profound awareness. Historically, floods and droughts have been called calamities, implying that they are not frequent occurrences. In the past, such widespread and severe disasters occurred only every few decades or even centuries. Now, only three years have passed since the last major disaster, and we face another one. This is definitely not due to changes in the climate or geography; it is due to the lack of human effort. If, since the establishment of the Republic of China, we had properly managed essential policies such as water conservancy and forestry, and if the local people had maintained the canals, dikes, and sluices with sincere effort, we would not be experiencing such frequent and increasingly severe disasters. Now, at this time of deep pain and loss, if we do not awaken with a sense of urgency and take immediate action to save ourselves, our nation will have no way to survive in this world. I recently telegraphed the provinces along the Yangtze River, calling for the mobilization of refugees to build dikes and dredge rivers, using labor as a form of relief. This is merely a temporary measure to address the symptoms. To eradicate disasters and remedy the future, we must have a widespread, concrete, and sustained effort throughout the country. It is my hope that the provincial governors will regard essential policies related to farmland water conservancy, such as cultivating forests, dredging rivers and lakes, constructing and protecting dikes and dams, and assisting in the construction of national water conservancy projects, as the most urgent priorities of their administration. Furthermore, the people in all regions should, without being urged, regularly repair and maintain the ditches, rivers, dikes, and dams in their respective villages, as these are all beneficial for water storage, drainage, and irrigation. We should also actively plant trees to regulate water and drought and improve the soil. Other matters related to disaster prevention and preparedness should also be diligently pursued. Only by planning ahead can we avoid unforeseen major disasters. Also, only through consistent efforts across all regions can we easily accomplish our goals. Take this flood as an example: if the waterways and dikes in the interior of each province were intact and well-maintained, even if disasters occurred, their severity would certainly be reduced. For instance, Jiangsu Province was fortunate to avoid flooding this year despite being inundated by the Yangtze, Huai, and other major rivers. This is undoubtedly due to the effective efforts of the provincial government and the people in recent years in water conservancy. This shows that human effort can overcome nature and eliminate disasters. Self-reliance is essential. This is not merely a matter of common interest; it is a matter of life and death. This is what the officials, merchants, and people of all provinces in our country should earnestly strive for. The severity of our country's economic crisis has already reached its limit. In the first half of this year, the trade deficit reached over 280 million. Both urban and rural areas are showing signs of decline and collapse. Adding to this the recent floods, according to the report of the Relief Commission, the number of victims in Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces alone exceeds ten million, and the public and private losses are no less than 500 million. Moreover, the situation in Henan and Shandong provinces is no less severe. I deeply believe that the fundamental crisis facing China today lies in the devastation of the national economy. The people's livelihood is increasingly impoverished, and the fate of the nation is precarious. Therefore, the only urgent task today is to concentrate the thoughts and efforts of the entire nation to save this declining economy. After this flood, it is even more apparent that national economic construction is an urgent task that brooks no delay. Truly, any nation can only survive by being diligent, self-improving, and enduring hardship. The right to exist in the world depends on this. Whether a nation prospers or declines depends on its efforts to control nature and overcome its environment. There are many reasons for China's economic stagnation and exhaustion today. However, we cannot blame the past due to the long-standing nature of these problems, nor can we give up and await our fate due to the difficulties of the internal and external environment. We must recognize reality, strive for solutions, consider what is possible, and make the greatest effort. While basic construction related to national survival should be led by the central government, national economic construction aimed at solving the people's livelihood problems must rely on the concrete promotion by local governments and the united efforts of all the people in order to succeed. The essential points are eightfold: First, promote conscripted labor. This is the foundation of all national economic construction, and it is especially important for water conservancy and transportation. We must break the people's long-standing habits of laziness and selfishness, encourage the virtues of labor, service, and mutual assistance, and promote increased production. All projects that are related to local production and welfare and require a large amount of labor, such as building roads, dredging rivers, constructing dikes, repairing dams, cultivating forests, and opening up reclaimed land, should be carried out through the conscripted labor system. The government must plan ahead, first through publicity, then through guidance, and ensure thorough preparation and thoughtful consideration. The people should regard participation in voluntary labor as their national duty and enthusiastically participate. This is the first point. Second, revitalize agriculture. We must actively promote all efforts to improve farming methods, increase agricultural production, invigorate agricultural finance, facilitate the smooth distribution of agricultural products, reduce the burden on farmers, and promote rural cooperation, with the initial goal of achieving self-sufficiency in food. On the one hand, we should strive to encourage land reclamation and animal husbandry, investigate abandoned land, mountains, forests, and plains, determine what is suitable for each area, urge land reclamation, transform barren land into arable land, cultivate forests to increase timber production, or engage in animal husbandry to increase the number of cattle and horses. For projects that are suitable for the use of collective labor, we should organize large-scale immigration and land reclamation or organize military-agricultural settlements, with the goal of leaving no land uncultivated. This is the third point. Fourth, regulate consumption. We should collect statistics on the types and quantities of consumer goods in various regions, especially in rural areas, and work with local professional organizations and cooperatives to strive for a balance between supply and demand. For goods that must be consumed, we should try to produce them as much as possible. For goods that cannot be produced, we should try to conserve their consumption as much as possible, in order to reduce the outflow of funds from the inland rural areas. Furthermore, we should improve the people's livelihoods to promote reasonable consumption. This is the fourth point. Fifth, revitalize industry. While various regions may be limited by their financial and material resources and unable to undertake large-scale industrial construction projects, the government, people, technicians, and entrepreneurs should work together to maintain and improve existing industries and handicrafts. At the same time, we must also promote simple industries that produce goods needed in rural areas, as well as industries that process agricultural products. This is the fifth point. Sixth, develop mineral resources. We should investigate the amount of mineral resources accumulated in various regions and the actual conditions of their extraction, eliminate superstition and ignorance among the people, remove the restrictions and destruction suffered by mine operators, guide and improve primitive and unsuitable mining methods, actively encourage investment in mineral resources, and support the independent operation and development of mine merchants, in order to open up natural resources and accommodate a large amount of labor. This is the sixth point. Seventh, facilitate the flow of goods. On the one hand, we should strive to develop road transportation between counties and provinces, improve water and land transportation, and remove transportation difficulties to facilitate the flow of goods. On the other hand, we should establish packaging and marketing organizations for various important agricultural products. This is the seventh point. Eighth, adjust finance. We should encourage savings among the people, facilitate the flow of funds, establish a complete rural lending system, promote credit cooperation to curb the exploitation of high interest rates, and guide the people to support the national policy on currency exchange. This is the eighth point. The above eight points are all practical measures that are essential for saving the current economic construction. The main point is to make the best use of human resources and land resources, and to bring all the forces of agriculture, industry, commerce, and education in various regions into close relationship with natural resources and economic undertakings. Therefore, the responsibility for presiding over and promoting this lies with the government. However, in order to achieve concrete and effective results, it is even more important that the local people have a general awareness, and that intellectuals take on the responsibility of promoting, guiding, and assisting in the organization. From this perspective, the investigation, statistics, collection of materials, research, and guidance on implementation methods in various regions are indispensable. Therefore, at the beginning of the process, we must, on the one hand, gather local experts to take on the task of specialized technical research and guidance, and on the other hand, train a large number of mid-level service personnel to take on the responsibility of investigation and general management and guidance. These so-called mid-level service personnel include civil servants from various agencies and public offices, village chiefs, and officers at all levels in the military. They can be trained in various ways according to their nature, without necessarily recruiting them separately. In order to achieve the goal of cooperation, it is also necessary for educational institutions, schools, groups, industries, national organizations, and cooperatives in various regions to enthusiastically support the effort. In short, government offices must abandon the past practice of perfunctory work that is unrealistic and only deals with superficialities. The people must deeply realize that this undertaking is the key to saving lives and turning the tide, and do their best to achieve the same goal. In the future, those who are responsible for construction administration in various provinces must earnestly focus on developing the national economy when formulating policy guidelines and regard this as the sole focus. If the government and the people respond as one, and work hard together with perseverance, I believe that there is hope for saving the endangered national economy, and that the material foundation for national revival will be laid. At this time of severe disaster, the fear of economic collapse is even greater. It is imperative to take timely remedial measures without delay. I sincerely hope that the officials of various provinces and the compatriots throughout the country will accept my humble words and put them into practice. Chiang Chung-cheng. (Eleventh, Central News Agency dispatch)

Fujian Provincial Government Requests Central Government to Allocate Funds for Disaster Relief

At the same time, there was also flooding in Changtai, with over 200 houses collapsing, resulting in a loss of 300,000 yuan, including crop losses. (Twelfth, Special Dispatch)

Headquarters Orders Hubei Provincial Government to Pay Attention to Locust Swarm Spread

(Hankou) The Headquarters ordered the provincial government that the locust plague is extremely serious, and if prevention and control are neglected, the consequences will be dire. Flying locusts have recently been discovered in Qichun. If they spread to various counties and neighboring provinces, it is feared that it will lead to a major disaster. The provincial government is instructed to propose methods for controlling locusts, strictly supervise the counties to eliminate them, and if necessary, conscript labor or request the assistance of resident military teams to quickly carry out the task. (Twelfth, Special Dispatch)

Central Figure of the Control Faction in the Japanese Military, Nagata Tetsuzan, Assassinated and Dies; Active-Duty Lieutenant Colonel Used a Military Sword to Commit the Crime and Was Arrested; Reminiscent of the Situation at the Time of the May 15th Incident

(Tokyo) The Ministry of the Army announced that Nagata Tetsuzan, the Director of the Military Affairs Bureau, was stabbed with a military sword this morning in his office by a certain lieutenant colonel from a certain unit, and his life is in critical condition. The perpetrator was immediately arrested by the military police. It is reported that Major General Nagata is a central figure in the Control Faction under Army Minister Hayashi. Nan, Abe, Honjo, Watanabe, and other military advisors are on its outer perimeter. (Thirteenth, Japanese United News dispatch)

(Tokyo) Tatsujiro Funatsu, director of general affairs for the Japan Cotton Spinners' Association in China, has returned after completing his survey of North China. The results indicate that if Japan wants to monopolize the North China cotton cloth market and develop Japan's textile industry in China, it should start cotton cultivation in North China, focusing on Hebei Province, and gradually develop the Japanese spinning industry in North China, centering on Beijing and Tianjin. At the same time, new factories should be established in the Beijing-Tianjin area to increase spindles in order to expand sales channels. Mr. Funatsu's proposals have been discussed with Japanese cotton textile industrialists many times and have been endorsed by them, and efforts will be actively promoted to realize them. Mr. Funatsu pointed out the reasons why Japan must develop the cotton textile industry in North China in the future, as follows:

(1) Factories in Shanghai and Qingdao have reached saturation;

(2) Sales channels for products from North China have always been the top in the whole of China;

(3) The political situation in North China will be relatively easier for the development of the textile industry in the future;

(4) Chinese workers in the Beijing-Tianjin area are docile and wages are low;

(5) Land prices are also low, leaving ample room for expansion of factories;

(6) The most important water volume and water quality for textile operations are also good;

(7) In a decade or two, North China can supply the best cotton raw materials;

(8) The general industry and transportation in the Beijing-Tianjin area are still relatively developed, and there are many possibilities for expanding sales channels to the interior. Moreover, there is little hope for cotton improvement in North China in the next five to ten years, so the construction of new factories must focus on ten to twenty years from now. In the future, Beijing and Tianjin will definitely become the center of the East Asian textile industry. (Hualian News Agency, 12th)

Current Status of US Cotton Exports to Japan - Accounts for 48 Percent

San Francisco - Ms. Milan, a researcher at the U.S. Pacific Council, published an article today stating that American farmers who grow long-staple cotton do not need to worry about losing the Japanese market. Although Japan is currently trying to cultivate cotton outside the United States, its needs still cannot help but rely on the United States. Although India, China, and Latin America all produce cotton, it is difficult to replace the position of the United States. The advantages of American cotton cannot be achieved urgently by new cotton varieties. Japanese cotton mills are accustomed to using American cotton and cannot use cotton from other producing areas for experimentation. Moreover, it is doubtful whether the new cotton growers, who need cotton urgently, can supply Japan with surplus cotton. Therefore, even if Japan is about to abandon American cotton, it must go through a very long period. According to statistics, in 1934, American cotton imported into Japan accounted for 55% of the total, and also accounted for 48% of Japan's total cotton imports. Indian cotton still ranked second. Japan's cotton purchases from countries other than the United States and India accounted for only 10% of the total, which is less than 1% more than in the previous four years. From 1931 to 1934, the total value of American cotton textile exports was US$1,062,000, while cotton exports to Japan increased by US$36,913,000 during the same period. Therefore, the increase in Japanese cotton textile exports did not have much impact on American goods. Moreover, cotton textiles accounted for only 2% of the total U.S. exports in 1934, while cotton accounted for 17%. (Kokumin News Agency, 11th)

Soviet Union Pardons Large Number of Former Offenders

(Moscow) When the grain tax was implemented in 1932 and 1933, some officials not only failed to prohibit the wealthy peasants from evading their obligations, but even violated their duties. Their absenteeism and dereliction of duty were obviously harmful to the interests of the state. At that time, these people were transferred for disciplinary action and sentenced to various punishments. This matter was a serious lesson for state officials, and administrative discipline was greatly enhanced as a result. The Soviet Central Executive Committee now believes that the motives of these offenders were not out of selfishness, and that most of the cases were due to their failure to understand the duties they were responsible for. Therefore, the Central Executive Committee now issues an order that these people may be exempted from punishment in the future. In addition, those who were convicted in 1933 and 1934 for privately issuing labor bonds and other currency substitutes have also been released. All records of crimes and all restrictions on their rights will be canceled for those who have been released by this order. (TASS, 12th)

It is said that he spent US$200,000 to marry eighty wives, but after marriage, he defrauded the women of their money and then abandoned them. (Kokumin News Agency, 11th)

Japanese Plane Flies Over Taiyuan

(Taiyuan) A Japanese plane flew over Taiyuan along the Zhengtai Railway at approximately 3:00 PM today, flying around the city twice, and then landed briefly at the North Gate airfield before flying northeast. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

U.S. Silver Purchase Reaching Its End; Silver Advocates Believe Government Only Implementing Part of the Plan; Congress Adjourns, No Other Hope

(Washington) With the closing date of Congress approaching, silver advocate members have completely given up hope of making silver the standard of the currency system. Today, according to the Associated Press, they believe that the government's silver purchase program is only implementing a portion of the original intention of the Silver Purchase Act. Representative Deyki stated that, in his opinion, the silver purchase plan is indeed a factor in raising wholesale prices, but its power to promote the export of agricultural products is very limited, because the Treasury Department's silver purchase has not fully met the wishes of Congress. Mr. Bao also stated that he agreed with Mr. Thomas that if the United States purchased enough silver to reach a ratio of three parts gold to one part silver, it would have to pay a price of one dollar per ounce. Deyki does not hope for the realization of a future international conference to discuss silver, but he believes that countries around the world are gradually realizing the value of silver as a medium of international exchange, because all the world's cash has been concentrated in a few countries, so there is no other "hard currency" besides silver. Currently, members of Congress have received many letters regarding silver, indicating an increase in public interest in silver. Most of these letters come from the western agricultural and mining areas, but most members do not believe that the silver issue can become a point of contention in next year's general election. Deyki also expressed opposition today to McKallen's proposal to restore the New York silver market, because this proposal would allow a few speculators to make huge profits. However, after the Treasury Department purchases enough silver, he would also support restoring the New York market. (Eleventh National Telegram)

Bandits Active at Various Passes of the Great Wall; Prevention Proves Difficult

(Beiping) Reports received from relevant sources indicate that the number of bandits at Jiafengkou is increasing daily, and they move around unpredictably, making incursions from here and there. The local garrison special police are finding it quite difficult to prevent them. The two hundred or so bandits recently discovered at Qiangzilu in Miyun County have been forced to flee to Baimaguan due to the effective prevention by the special police. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Bandits are causing disturbances in the Xihefengkou area of Miyun, robbing everywhere, kidnapping, and burning houses. Residents are fleeing to the county town of Miyun to take refuge. The Second Squadron Leader of the Miyun Special Police, Zi Zhenhua, led his entire squadron to pursue and suppress the bandits in the Hefengkou area. The bandits, unable to withstand the pressure, began to retreat towards Sancha in the Rehe territory. By 10 a.m., the special police had completely recovered the Hefengkou area. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

(Tianjin) At around 2 p.m. on the eleventh, more than two hundred bandits, fleeing from outside the Great Wall passes, arrived at the Hefengkou area of Huairou and Miyun counties, creating a great stir. Deng Wenhan's troops from the Miyun Security Corps are already fiercely suppressing them. Groups of bandits on foot and horseback have also been discovered in the Dongqiangzilu and Dashuiyu areas of Miyun, seemingly intending to attack the Kulishixia Town and Baimaguan areas. Wang Bolin, the magistrate of Miyun County, has ordered the local militia to intercept them. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Bandit activity at various passes of the Great Wall has not yet subsided. Bandits frequently appear and harass the Jiafengkou area, with varying numbers and unpredictable movements, making prevention quite difficult. More than six hundred scattered bandits were also discovered in the southeast of Qiangzilu in Miyun County on the tenth. Due to the strict precautions taken, they fled towards Baimaguan. (Twelfth Central News Agency Telegram)

(Beiping) The Ao Yu District Commissioner's Office, in order to thoroughly eliminate bandit troubles in the war zone, has decided to convene the captains of the first, second, and third Jing police squads, Zhang Yantian, Zhang Qingyu, and Li Haitian, etc., around the 20th of this month in Tangshan to discuss bandit suppression and joint defense matters. The county magistrates of the counties near the Great Wall will also go to Tangshan to participate in the discussions. It is reported that Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu have decided to go to Tangshan within the next week. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Reporters Petition Delegation from Various Counties in Jiangsu Arrives in Nanjing Yesterday

(Nanjing) A petition delegation of news reporters from various counties in Jiangsu, represented by Sun Dexian and 28 others, arrived in Nanjing from Wuxi on the morning of the twelfth. In the afternoon, they hosted the Beijing New Journalism Circles, reporting the reasons for requesting the amendment of the new Publication Law. They are scheduled to go to the Legislative Yuan and the Judicial Yuan on the thirteenth, and to the Central Party Headquarters on the fourteenth to petition. (Twelfth Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) Colleagues in the press from various counties in Jiangsu Province have jointly come to Nanjing to request the Central Government to reconsider and amend the Publication Law, and to seek relief regarding the Publication Law and defamation crimes in the Criminal Law, and to determine the penalty for reporters' negligence as a single crime. They gathered in Wuxi on the 11th, and the participating colleagues from Wuxi were Wu Guanli, Sun Xiangfeng, Sun Dexian, and Hua E; the representatives from Wujin were Chen Kehua, Bu Hezhi, Tu Zhifang, and Ye Xinhe; the representatives from Yixing and Liyang were Fang Zhiyuan; the representatives from Jiangyin were Cao Yichen and Xi Xiaohua; the representatives from Zhenjiang were Bao Mingshu, Yang Hanmei, Zhang Yishan, and Yin Techang; the representatives from Wuxian were Hu Juemin and Yan Yisheng; the representatives from Changshu were Zhao Buqiu (representing his wife), Kong Xiangzhen, and Zhou Zhenhua; the representative from Nantong was Zhang Jianren; the representative from Haimen was Gong Jieping; and the representatives from Jiangdu were Zhang Zhiqing, Bu Runquan, Li Yintang, and Zhang Jichuan. A total of 25 counties participated in signing the petition, 8 in the name of the reporters' association, and 40 in the name of the newspapers. 15 counties did not participate in the petition. There were over 30 people in total. They arrived in Nanjing at 7 a.m. on the morning of the twelfth and stayed at the Central Hotel. At 5 p.m., they hosted the capital's press and reporters stationed in Nanjing from national newspapers, including Cheng Cangbo, Tang Ren'an, Wang Gongtao, Chen Mingde, Tang Zhi, Yu Shuli, Liao Shouchang, Kong Zhaokai, Shen Jiuxiang, Zhao Ying, and Cheng Qi, etc., over 30 people. The members of the delegation's presidium, Sun Dexian, Bao Mingshu, Hu Juemin, Wu Guanli, Sun Xiangfeng, and Hua E, took their seats. After Cheng Cangbo introduced them, the chairman, Sun Dexian, stood up and addressed the audience, saying that over 16 reporters' associations and over 40 newspapers from Jiangsu had sent 32 representatives to Nanjing, and the purpose of the petition was twofold: first, the Publication Law was strictly restrictive and difficult to implement; second, the defamation and slander clauses in the Criminal Law did not provide sufficient protection for journalists, and they requested relief. They were willing to work hard with the leadership of the capital's press to petition the administrative authorities and hoped that the capital's leading figures would provide guidance so that they could follow. Then, Bao Mingshu stood up and explained in detail how the inland news industry was being greatly affected by the restrictions of the Publication Law, and that the future of public opinion should be expanded. As the capital was in a leading position, he respectfully sought guidance. Next, Yu Shuli stood up and reported on the passage of the Publication Law in the Legislative Yuan, and advocated uniting and continuing the petition. Then, Tang Zhi spoke, hoping that the national press should unite and work together to increase their strength and fight together. Finally, they agreed on the next steps: the Jiangsu Petition Delegation, the Nanjing Journalism Association, and those established in Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, Tianjin, and Nanjing would each send four representatives to form a temporary joint organization to be responsible for further petitioning matters. Yu Shuli, Chen Mingde, Cao Ren'an, and Sun Dexian were publicly designated as conveners to collect materials, organize the main points of the petition, and submit them to the authorities. Three, to prepare for a national press association in a short time. They adjourned at 7 p.m. The entire delegation is scheduled to visit the Executive Yuan, the Central Propaganda Department, the Ministry of Interior, the Courts, and the Judicial Yuan on the morning of the thirteenth to petition, and to pay their respects at the Mausoleum in the afternoon. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Provisional Notarization Regulations Promulgated

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan has recently promulgated provisional notarization regulations, consisting of three chapters and a total of forty-seven articles. These regulations stipulate notarization methods, one being the creation of notarization documents, and the other being the authentication of private documents. Applicants requesting notarization should pay a notarization fee. It is currently awaiting the Ministry of Justice to formulate fee regulations, and then it will first be trialed in Shanghai. After it is effective, it will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan in accordance with legislative procedures to enact a notarization law and implement it nationwide. (Twelfth Central News Agency Telegram)

International Business Telegraph - Reuters Special Business Telegram, August 12th -

Gold and Silver

London gold price in the UK today is 140 shillings and 4 pence, unchanged. The London silver market in the UK is quiet, with the spot price at 30 pence and 125, and the futures price at 30 pence and 1875, both down by 0.0625. The United States is buying, and India and China are selling. The market closed quietly.

Exchange Rates

The London foreign exchange market in the UK was very quiet today. The price of the pound sterling remained practically unchanged. The opening exchange rate between the UK and the US was 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 6 fen, 9375, down 0.0615 compared to the last closing price between the US and the UK. It rose by 0.0625 within the first hour, fell at 10 o'clock, rose again at 1 o'clock, and rose again by 0.0625 at 2 o'clock, making it 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 7 fen, 0625.

The opening price between the UK and France was 74 francs 97, up four pound sounds, fell three pound sounds at noon, making it 74 francs 94, and remained unchanged at 2 o'clock.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened lower for three reasons: (1) Liverpool prices were low, (2) the weather in the cotton-growing areas was still good, and (3) there was no good news regarding cotton loans, and it was feared that there would be a lot of selling. The opening market situation was still manageable because industry players bought in a little. Generally, there is now progress in the business.

UK Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market in the UK fell due to continued good weather in the United States and a lack of news on cotton loans. At 1 p.m. in the afternoon, the October futures price was 5.97, down 6 pound sounds compared to the closing price on Saturday.

UK Wheat: The sudden change in wheat prices in Chicago on Saturday caused retail investors to close out positions, so the Liverpool wheat market in the UK opened lower. At 1 p.m. in the afternoon, the October futures price was 5 shillings, 2 pence, and 25, down 875.

US Wheat: Chicago wheat opened this morning, and prices were mixed and lower. Many merchants are temporarily not receiving prices because the Canadian government's wheat production report will be released today. It is expected that this estimate will be favorable to the multi-party side, but there is a lot of selling, and Russia's position is also making people fearful. Grains also fell in price because the weather report and production news remained good.

Rubber

London: London rubber prices were stable this morning. At noon, the transaction prices for October and November futures were 5 pence 875, the same as the Friday closing price.

New York: New York rubber opened a few pound sounds higher this morning. Although the market is not weak, prices are still stable. According to industry estimates, manufacturers' demand will increase for a long time.

Securities

The New York stock market opened stably this morning. Although prices fluctuated greatly later due to a large amount of profit-taking, the market was still strong. Prices rose uniformly at the beginning of the opening, but those that have risen the most recently have seen the most profit-taking, so the prices of stocks for car utilities and department stores have all fallen below Saturday's closing price. Railway stocks are strong, and oil stocks are stable. The Dow Jones average of 30 industrial stocks opened at 128.63, up 69 pound sounds. The prices are as follows:

Anesthetic Method Should Be Used for Executing Death Row Inmates to Reduce Suffering

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Judicial Administration has ordered the chief prosecutors of the high courts of each province to investigate death row sentences, which are the most painful of punishments. Improper execution methods make the suffering even more unbearable. Judicial organs used to use chloroform water to cause the prisoner to lose consciousness before execution in order to avoid pain, which was a good intention. The Ministry originally stipulated that executions should be carried out by hanging and, as far as possible, an anesthetic method should be used before execution to reduce suffering. This was previously ordered and circulated for compliance. The Ministry has now ordered the Institute of Forensic Medicine to select four commonly used anesthetic drugs, 1. ether, 2. chloroform, 3. yobane, 4. ethyl chloride, and explain the application methods. A separate list has been submitted. The chief prosecutor should inform the order and instruct the use, in order to emphasize humanitarianism. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Kuling: Record of Recovering the Leased Territory. Provincial Government Sends Officials for Successful Negotiation. Official Signing and Return of Sovereignty.

Kuling Correspondence: After the recovery of police power in January of the 16th year of the Republic of China in the foreign leased territory of Kuling, Lushan, the internal affairs, finance, public works, sanitation and other administrations of the area were still controlled by the board of directors formed by foreigners and executed by the Kuling Public Affairs Office. After several negotiations, on the 8th of this month, the British Consul Morse officially signed with the Director of the Lushan Administration Bureau to return the administration and restore our sovereignty. The process is as follows: Lushan is the only famous scenic spot in the southeast, close to the Yangtze River, with convenient transportation. Celebrated figures and scholars of all dynasties have roamed and composed poems here, adding to its beauty. In the late Qing Dynasty, the German merchant, Schill von Rennenkampff, illicitly sold a piece of land in Kuling, the northern part of the mountain, to a Briton named Liddell. Liddell then cleared the land and built houses, causing an uproar among the local people, who, not understanding diplomatic procedures, burned down Liddell's residence. The British Minister lodged a protest, and the Qing government, fearing the power of foreigners, agreed to pay compensation and apologize. The Dehua County Office then formally leased Changchong to Liddell as a summer resort on November 16th of the 22nd year of the Guangxu reign. The area is over 4,000 feet above sea level, and the northern gap has Poyang Lake, which regulates the Yangtze River's water vapor, keeping the summer temperature around 80 degrees Fahrenheit, about 15 degrees cooler than the plains, making it ideal for summer rest. The famous scenic spots, historical sites, flying waterfalls, and flowing springs are especially suitable for regulating the body and mind. Therefore, foreigners have worked hard to develop this area, building roads, constructing foreign houses, and making it increasingly prosperous. Later, they expanded it from time to time, incorporating Caodipo, Xiachong, Houziling, Doctor's Knoll, and other places into the leased area. Covering several miles, it is full of villas and foreign buildings. At that time, the authorities turned a blind eye to this, and foreigners formed a board of directors, with twelve directors elected by residents from Britain, Germany, and the United States. Underneath was the Kuling Public Affairs Office, which carried out all administrative matters related to police, finance, public works, and public health, essentially forming a concession that only paid us 711 yuan in rent per year. Even the police bureau and land survey bureau from the Qing Dynasty to the 15th year of the Republic could not overstep it. It is reported that in the early years of the Republic of China, the land in Kuling was less than two or three jiao per square zhang. Between the 7th and 8th years, the price of land soared as many people came here for summer retreats. By the 15th year, each square zhang cost from four or five yuan to as much as twenty-five or six yuan. Foreigners made a fortune here, while our countrymen who came here for summer retreats, to set up shops, or to reside were excluded to the Zhengjie Yaowo Shiba Ling area. Even if they owned land and houses in the leased territory, they were not allowed to participate in any of the so-called administrative rights of the board of directors. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, the concessions of Hankou and Jiujiang were recovered one after another, but in Kuling, only the police power was returned. The board of directors still existed in a deformed state, and the administration of the Public Affairs Office remained the same as before. According to a survey in the 17th year of the Republic of China, the Public Affairs Office collected tens of thousands of yuan annually in taxes from residents, which were entirely at its disposal. Although we recovered police power, the Public Affairs Office only assisted with police salaries of 283 yuan per month and 200 yuan for the security police team. In the 19th year of the Republic, the Xun Municipal Government abolished the Lushan Administration Bureau, which became directly under the provincial government. Vigorously reforming and improving public safety, public works, sanitation, public utilities, and other aspects, foreigners could find no excuse to object. Therefore, the director of the Bureau, Jiang Zhicheng, following the instructions of his superiors, repeatedly negotiated to recover all administration and take over the Public Affairs Office, to avoid being a mere figurehead. Only this summer did some progress appear. When the Chairman of the Provincial Government, Xiong Shihui, arrived on the mountain this month, he immediately telegraphed Commissioner Xiao of the Provincial Government to come and negotiate with the British Consul. As a result, the various leased territories in Kuling were recovered. At 11 a.m. on the 8th, the Director of the Lushan Administration Bureau, Jiang Zhicheng, and the British Consul, Morse, officially signed the agreement. Thus, this leased territory, from November 16th of the 21st year of the Guangxu reign to the present day, thirty-nine years later, has been completely resolved. (August 9th)

Hangzhou: Holding Province-Wide Business Registration

In order to control and manage the businesses of the entire province, to adapt supply and demand, and to eliminate speculation and fraud, the Zhejiang Provincial Business Administration Bureau plans to hold a general business registration, investigate the organizational content of each store, the exact amount of capital, etc. A plan has been drafted and submitted to the Construction Department to be presented to the Provincial Government Meeting for approval, so that it can be implemented. The principles are as follows: (1) Registration will be based on the principle of not charging fees. Even if a very small fee is charged, it will be borne by the Chamber of Commerce. (2) Emphasis will be placed on the rights and interests of registration and strict measures against non-registration, so that merchants will be happy to engage in it. (3) New stores cannot begin operations until they are registered.

Two Railway Party Headquarters Launch: Party Members Donate for Disaster Relief. Railway Bureau Yesterday Instructed All Departments to Assist. Drafted Flood Relief Fundraising Measures.

The two railway special party headquarters, in light of the unprecedented catastrophe of floods in Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi this year, have launched a general mobilization for disaster relief fundraising. The New News Agency reporter hereby transcribes the railway bureau's instructions and fundraising measures as follows:

Railway Bureau Instructions

The Two Railways Administration Bureau yesterday instructed all departments, stating, "It is approved that the executive committee of this railway special party headquarters has sent a letter stating that our country has long suffered from natural disasters and man-made calamities. The floods of the 20th year are still a scene of devastation, and this year's floods in Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi are an unprecedented catastrophe. The displaced compatriots are in dire straits and cannot bear to see. The loss of property directly affects the national economy and the people's livelihood and is even more difficult to estimate. Our party takes universal love as the revolutionary motive, and disaster relief and compassion for the people as our duty. As the ancients said, the heart of compassion is in everyone. We, as public officials under the party's rule, have always taken leading the masses and relieving their suffering as our responsibility. We must have the deepest sympathy for the general disaster-stricken people and do our best to fulfill our obligations. Our association has previously received a telegram from the central government ordering us to participate in disaster relief work, which has been forwarded to our subordinates for compliance. Now, after the 128th executive committee meeting of our association, it was resolved to launch a general mobilization for railway party members to donate to disaster relief. The detailed measures have also been drafted. In addition to forwarding them for compliance and reporting them, a copy of the measures is enclosed and sent to your bureau. Please investigate and instruct your subordinates to assist as much as possible when the time comes. This order is issued, and a copy of the measures is attached. The order should be followed by the relevant departments."

Fundraising Measures

Measures of the Kuomintang Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Party for Fundraising for Disaster Relief in Various Regions of China: (1) The purpose of these measures is to provide relief for the floods along the Yellow River and Yangtze River in the 24th year of the Republic of China. (2) Fundraising will be organized by a fundraising team organized by the special party headquarters, which will be responsible for handling it in various districts. (3) The organizational system of the fundraising team is as follows: (1) All executive and supervisory committee members and secretaries of the special party headquarters are the chief team leaders. (2) All executive and supervisory committee members of each district party headquarters are the district team leaders. (3) All executive committee members of each district branch are the district platoon leaders. (4) Party members and probationary party members of this railway are all members of the fundraising team. (5) All staff members of this railway special party headquarters are secretaries of the fundraising team. (6) Each chief team leader must undertake to raise at least 5 yuan in national currency, each team member must undertake to raise at least 2 yuan in national currency, and each secretary must undertake to raise at least 10 yuan in national currency. (The above regulations are the minimum amounts. Those who can raise more money will be rewarded by the executive committee of the special party headquarters.) (7) The awards for the fundraising team will be based on the following two standards: (1) Based on the best fundraising performance of each platoon. (2) Based on the best fundraising performance of individuals. (8) Those who have already served as chief team leaders, district team leaders, or platoon leaders are not required to serve as team members for fundraising. (9) Those whose fundraising amount is less than the amount stipulated in Article 6 must still make up the difference. (10) Fundraising receipts will be issued by the special party headquarters. If they are not sufficient, a request can be made for additional issuance. (11) This fundraising work should be completed within one month. (12) After the fundraising period expires, all fundraising personnel should send the stubs of the fundraising receipts, together with the donations, level by level to the special party headquarters, which will forward them to the central government for distribution. (13) After the fundraising is completed, the special party headquarters should announce the names and amounts of the donors in the Two Railways Weekly to show good faith. (14) Fundraising team secretaries will not receive any public funds for official travel, as it is entirely voluntary work. (15) These measures will be implemented after being approved by the executive committee of the special party headquarters.

Central Trust Bureau to Receive Spring Order. China Industrial Bank's Prize Savings. China-France Savings Society to be Completely Received. Universal Savings Society Has Decided on Measures. Date of Trust Bureau Opening Not Decided.

The New Voice News Agency reports that the Central Bank Trust Bureau Preparatory Office, after receiving the China-France Savings Society, the China Industrial Bank Savings Department's special prize savings has also been ordered to be transferred. The case of the Universal Savings Society has been agreed upon. The bureau is about to open. The details are as follows.

Receiving China-France: Nearing Completion

After the China-France Savings Society was ordered by the Ministry of Finance on July 3 to be completely transferred to the Central Bank Trust Bureau, the Central Bank Trust Bureau Preparatory Office sent personnel to receive it separately. Because the society's head office and branches are spread across the country, although the initial reception has been completed, the review of the society's assets and liabilities has not yet been completed. After completion, it will be handled by the Trust Bureau. It is reported that the society's assets and liabilities can offset each other. According to the loan balance sheet as of the end of the 21st year of the Republic of China, both the asset amount and the liability amount are 4,392,148 yuan, 8 jiao, and 3 fen.

China Industrial Bank's Prize Savings: Ordered to be Transferred

The China Industrial Bank Savings Department established a special prize savings in the 22nd year of the Republic of China with 100,000 numbers as one session. Each number pays 30 yuan at once, and the stipulated period is eight years. Upon expiration, in addition to returning the principal, each number is given an interest of 4 yuan and 1 jiao. The lottery is drawn every three months. After 32 times, it is completely full. More than 61,000 numbers have joined, totaling more than 1.8 million yuan. Soon after, it was ordered to stop accepting new customers, but those who have already joined will continue until the eight-year term expires. Now the bank has been ordered by the Ministry of Finance to transfer the closed prize savings of the Savings Society to the Central Trust Bureau for handling. At the same time, the bureau's preparatory office has been ordered to receive it.

Universal Savings Society: Disposal Measures The Universal Savings Society stopped operating its branches in various parts of China on July 1, but the Shanghai General Association, as well as the Guangzhou, Hankou, Beiping, Tianjin, and Qingdao branches, continue to operate as usual. As for the lottery draw on the 15th of each month, it is also held as usual. The Ministry of Finance, because the laws and regulations promulgated by the government stipulate that prize savings are prohibited, in addition to transferring the China-France Savings Society and the China Industrial Bank Prize Savings Department to the Central Trust Bureau for handling,

Trust Bureau: Preparing to Open

The Central Bank Trust Bureau, located on Hankou Road, has completed all arrangements. The director and deputy director have been decided. According to the New Voice News Agency reporter, the bureau is now actively preparing. As for the opening date, it has not yet been decided. It is expected to be implemented before the end of this month. The rumor of the 15th is probably due to insufficient preparation. In addition, the Ministry of Finance will guarantee the interests of the savings account holders of prize savings. The purpose of receiving the China-France Savings Society and the China Industrial Bank Prize Savings this time is to protect the interests of the savings account holders.

July: Shanghai Goods Exported to the United States Statistics: Increase Compared to Last Year

The Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reports that, according to statistics released by the US Consul General in Shanghai today (the 12th), Shanghai's exports to the US in July were worth a total of US$1,005,235. Last year, the same month had only US$607,400, so the increase is considerable. In the first seven months of this year, Shanghai's exports to the US were worth a total of US$9,774,183, while in the same period last year they were US$7,221,382. Shanghai's exports to the Philippine Islands in July saw a significant decrease, with a total of US$82,274. In the first seven months of this year, the total was US$569,989, while in July of last year it was US$1,161,21, and in the first seven months it was US$728,109. Shanghai's exports to Hawaii in July also saw a decrease, with a total of US$2,756. In the first seven months of this year, the total was US$27,752, while in July of last year it was US$4,146, and in the first seven months it was US$28,656. In the first half of this year, China's total exports to the United States were worth US$31,537,582, an increase of US$7,276,427 compared to the same period last year. China's total exports to the United States in June of this year were worth US$4,153,368, while in the same month last year they were US$3,030,906. In the first half of this year, 115,500 ounces of domestic silver were shipped to the United States, worth US$58,424.

Special Rent Reduction Committee: Rent Reduction Movement Week, from the 25th of This Month to the End

The Shanghai Special Rent Reduction Committee's first executive committee meeting resolved to hold a conference to revitalize the market and unify the rent reduction movement, scheduled for one week, from the 25th to the 31st of this month, named "Rent Reduction Movement Week." The standing members of the committee, such as Li Ao-kui, have drafted a plan, which will be handled and implemented by the publicity department. Excerpts of the committee's announcement to all citizens and the regulations passed for organizing rent reduction branches are recorded below:

Announcement to Citizens

The rent reduction announcement states: "Regarding rent reduction, it is not a thorough solution to social and economic problems, but when implemented in the current Shanghai society, it can be said to be an effective remedy for regulating the social economy and ensuring social peace and order. Regulating the social economy is not only for the sake of the common people but also for the wealthy. In large cities, industry and commerce are the focus. If industry and commerce decline, the city also declines. Currently, Shanghai society can be said to have declined to an extreme. A large number of bankrupt and unemployed people are being forced to leave Shanghai one after another, resulting in many vacant houses. Landlords would rather keep their houses empty than reduce rents. They really do not understand how to ensure social peace and order. The result of an unbalanced social economy is social unrest, leading to tragedies of crime. Reducing rents is the primary method for revitalizing the market and an important plan for solving people's livelihood problems. The environment is such, the facts are such, and the reasons are also such. The so-called rent reduction is to regulate the social economy, ensure social peace and order, and revive urban prosperity. Our citizens should all take responsibility, work on the rent reduction movement, and work together to achieve the goal of unified rent reduction. This is a special announcement." Shanghai Special Rent Reduction Committee.

Organizational Regulations

Regulations for Organizing Rent Reduction Associations: (1) These regulations are based on the resolution of the first committee meeting of the "Shanghai Special Rent Reduction Committee." (2) This committee (hereinafter referred to as the "Committee") is the general association for the Shanghai Special District and is divided into four districts, each with a district association: (1) Pudong District Association, (2) Puxi District Association, (3) Central District Association, (4) City Federation District Branch. Under the district association, branches may be established. Those organized by road are branch associations, and those organized by neighborhood are sub-branch associations. (3) Anyone initiating the organization of a district association must have several representatives elected by the branch associations apply for approval and registration with the Committee, and the organization department of the Committee will send personnel to provide guidance. (4) The number of members in each district branch association shall be limited to fifteen to twenty-five, and the method of election shall be determined according to the circumstances of each district. (5) Each City Federation District Association may send one representative to attend the Committee meeting. (6) Anyone organizing a district branch association must have several representatives elected by shops or households apply for approval with the Committee, and the Committee will notify the organization department and the district association to provide guidance. (7) The number of members in each district branch association shall be limited to seven to fifteen, and the method of election shall be determined according to the circumstances of each district branch association. (8) Each district branch association may send two representatives to attend the district association meeting. (9) Anyone initiating the organization of a sub-branch association must have several representatives elected by households or businesses in the neighborhood apply for approval and registration with the Committee, and the Committee will notify the organization department, the district association to which it belongs, and the branch association to provide guidance. (10) If the number of members in each sub-branch association is less than ten, it shall be jointly organized with neighboring sub-branch associations. (11) The number of members in each sub-branch association shall be limited to five to fifteen, and the method of election shall be determined according to the circumstances of each sub-branch association. (12) Each sub-branch association may send one to two representatives to attend the branch association meeting. (13) Separate detailed rules for the district associations and branches will be formulated. (14) These regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the Executive Committee of the Committee. (15) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended at any time.
