Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Association Hosted Factory Owners for the Second Time Yesterday: Requesting Factories to Genuinely Assist with Investigation Work; Representatives Zhou Yuantai and Others Expressed Willingness to Cooperate

The Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Committee of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce held its first reception for factory owners and representatives at the Chamber yesterday at 4:00 PM. Attendees included representatives from Kailin Paint Company, Zhongnan Factory, Zhenhua Paint Company, Tianyuan Condiment Factory, Jiuda Silk Factory, Hu Wanxing Iron Factory, Dashun Factory, Tianyuan Jiuji Monosodium Glutamate Factory, Shanghai First Foundry, Gongli Socks Factory, Huanyu Pharmaceutical Factory, Yaguang Manufacturing Company, Dongfang Nianhong Company, Jincheng Pottery Company, Huatong Electric Factory, and others. Xi Yushu and Xu Xiaochu, the director and deputy director of the investigation team, and Ren Jinping, the general secretary, warmly received the guests. At 4:30 PM,

Xi Yushu, the Chairman

Delivered a speech, stating: "Today is the second time our association is hosting factory owners and representatives. The purpose is to allow industry leaders to understand the significance of our association's preliminary work procedures so that we can cooperate in a spirit of mutual assistance and seek effective relief, so that the hope of industrial and commercial revitalization can gradually become a reality. Since ancient times, China's industrial and commercial enterprises have been mired in an environment of increasing import surpluses and outflow of silver, making development inherently difficult. Recently, the global economic crisis has swept over China again, coupled with the impact of the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, resulting in a sharp drop in land prices and a tightening of credit. The working capital used by industry and commerce for production has suddenly become scarce. Therefore, the production status of industry and commerce has shown an unprecedentedly tragic scene. If we do not seek relief urgently, we will inevitably move towards collapse, and both the national economy and the people's livelihood will be harmed. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, in view of this, has risen up and hired leaders and experts from various industries to work together. Viewed superficially, it may seem slow, but if we want to recover from fatigue and decline, we must not treat the superficial symptoms without addressing the underlying causes of the decline. It is like a patient who only asks the doctor to treat the external symptoms while concealing the internal causes of the disease, which will inevitably lead to a recurrence of the external symptoms. Today, our association invites you all to come here to cooperate in accordance with the preliminary work procedures, striving to identify the internal causes of the decline of industry and commerce, as well as the causes of these internal illnesses. As for the issues of stagnation of working capital, which are the external symptoms, we are also actively researching them and have not ignored them." Then,

Ren Jinping Presented

His views, stating: "The reasons for the decline of industry and commerce in our country today, in terms of external symptoms, are the dumping of foreign goods, the outflow of silver, the decline in land prices, the shortage of working capital, and the sharp drop in purchasing power, which are all well known. In terms of internal illnesses, the lack of sound economic and personnel organizations is also generally known. Therefore, we must conduct a thorough study of the causes of both external symptoms and internal illnesses. Now, I will just talk about the reasons for the unsound economic and personnel organizations of industry and commerce, based on my personal experience, for the education of those engaged in business today. Often, due to their own weak financial resources, they reduce expenses on management and employees, which leads to a situation where business is not progressing, personnel are in disarray, and the economy is insufficient. Other shortcomings arise from this. These shortcomings weaken the internal structure of the business, making it unable to defend against the aforementioned external attacks. Therefore, in my personal opinion, the meaning of managing a business is the same as governing a country. The goal of governing a country is twofold: internally, to ensure the safety of the people's lives, and externally, to defend against aggression. But to be able to defend against aggression, we must first ensure the safety of the people's lives. Otherwise, we will not only be unable to defend against external attacks, but we will also be unable to obtain assistance from others. Even if we obtain assistance, it will still be ineffective. For example, if an unemployed person needs 20 yuan per month to live on, but is unable to live due to economic difficulties and must rely on a loan for assistance, if someone lends him 100 yuan and he still does not engage in production, he will still be unable to live as before in the sixth month. Therefore, if industry and commerce expect to be rescued by others, they must study and eliminate the reasons that hinder their own production and demonstrate a spirit worthy of rescue, so that people believe that after obtaining rescue, they will be able to increase production. In this way, industry and commerce must urgently study the reasons that hinder their own production. The method of studying the reasons is to first emphasize statistics, so that the advantages and disadvantages of various situations can be analyzed by statistical methods.

I will cite a few examples to illustrate

(1) The time when the general manager or factory director arrives at the office is often after 11:00 AM, which shows that the general manager or factory director spends more than one hour of his thoughts, energy, and time every day, which means that the business reduces its ability to advance by more than one hour every day. (2) If the sales destination of a product is Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, it shows that the sales potential is not being fully realized, and the domestic market outside of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and the overseas markets outside the national boundary are being abandoned. (3) The differences between business operators and employees are examples, and the advantages and disadvantages of any other matter can be analyzed by statistical methods. Our association wants to ask you to analyze the advantages and disadvantages of the investigation work in detail and train the personnel to increase their ability. Therefore, if industry and commerce want to expect economic assistance, they must find ways to clearly distinguish between advantages and disadvantages and eliminate or reduce the causes of weakness in the internal structure of the business. If the internal structure of the business gradually becomes stronger and healthier, the business's credit will inevitably increase, and it will be easier to obtain economic assistance. After obtaining economic assistance, it can strive for the survival of the business internally and resist economic aggression externally." Finally, the survey forms were distributed, and representatives from various factories, such as Zhou Yuantai, expressed their sincerity in cooperating with the association. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

City Federation Branch: Contributing Opinions on Industrial and Commercial Revitalization: Requesting the Municipal Council to Reduce Land Prices, Banks Should Provide Loans with Domestic Goods as Collateral

Shanghai Special District City Federation 21st District Branch:

Shanghai Special District City Federation 21st District Branch, in view of the recession in all industries in Shanghai since the January 28th Incident and the lack of means to maintain them, the association has formulated opinions and sent a letter to the Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Committee for discussion. The original text states: "It is said that action is more valuable than words, and action is more valuable than eloquent rhetoric. This is an ancient saying. All matters, large or small, are based on practical action. Otherwise, the speaker is earnest, but the listener is dismissive. It is like the ancient proverb that says, 'Seek truth from facts, do not engage in empty talk.' Since the January 28th Incident, all industries in Shanghai have been declining and difficult to recover. The society is depressed, the economy is in panic, the countryside is bankrupt, and industry and commerce are struggling to survive. This is truly a time of crisis and survival. Enlightened people in our city deeply feel the difficulty of the situation and the collapse of all industries. They have organized the Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Committee, gathering leaders and experts from various industries to discuss and study the causes of the decline of all industries and the development plan, determine the plan, and assist in the implementation, so that things can be accomplished. Our colleagues in the association are very happy to hear this, believing that revitalizing industry and commerce is the most urgent task at present and cannot be delayed. According to the economic panic in our city in recent years, nothing is more serious than this. The causes are indeed several: (1) Property transfers and mortgages, one after another, repeatedly increasing the mortgage loans. Creditors, for the sake of interest, have to raise rents, and this burden is added to industry and commerce. At this time, the purchasing power of the bankrupt rural areas is not strong, especially for small industry and commerce, who are depleting their resources and unable to maintain themselves. Shops are closing down every day. This should be prevented. Anyone who has already mortgaged their property should not be allowed to transfer the mortgage again, in order to manipulate the situation. (2) Land prices in our city have been increasing year by year. Those with real estate have to raise rents due to the cost of building houses. In this situation, merchants and people are already overwhelmed and are crying for rent reduction, but the results are very few. The Municipal Council should be asked to reduce the land prices in the city to the lowest possible level. If this is implemented, then rents will be reduced without being reduced. To seek the revitalization of industry and commerce, this is the most important and fundamental issue that should be resolved immediately. (3) Banks are the financial hub of the city. The interest rate on loans should be reduced as much as possible, and should not exceed 7%, to reduce the burden on commerce. All banks should also quickly open up loans with domestic goods as collateral, stipulating a certain amount, or with a standard of 500 yuan or more and 1,000 yuan or less, so that the finances of small industry and commerce can be circulated and avoid the risk of being cut off from funds. Saving a part of industry and commerce can maintain the increase in domestic goods production. Without this, it is not worth considering other plans, because it is like disregarding the root and only focusing on the branches. Our association is aware of this and cannot remain silent. We hereby contribute our opinions."

Wax Industry Association Reports on the Situation: Factories and Kilns Must Use Domestic Goods to Reverse the Decline

The Shanghai Wax Industry Association, having previously received an order from the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau to investigate the status of the industry, has completed the investigation and submitted it to the Bureau for review yesterday by mail. The original report and investigation form are recorded below: (Report) A report on the submission of a report. On July 26th, the Bureau issued Order No. 6393, stating, "In order to rescue commerce, the Bureau previously prepared a Shanghai Business Situation Investigation Form and ordered all industry associations in April of this year to conduct a thorough investigation and discussion in accordance with the form and report back, with a deadline of one month. The association has been overdue for a long time. It is hereby ordered that the association promptly comply with the previous order and report in detail within fifteen days of receiving this document. Any delays will be punished." Having received this, we should comply with the previously received form, fill it out truthfully, and submit it separately. We hope that the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Wu, will review it and bestow his virtue. Respectfully submitted. "The current situation of the industry": (1) The changes and overview of business operations over the years. Although the wax industry has not changed over the years, during times of social tranquility and prosperity, it relied on the pure profits of business operations to cover various expenses. If there were surpluses, they were minimal. (2) The recent business situation and the reasons for its rise and fall. Since the January 28th Incident, the market has gradually declined, and prices have fluctuated, resulting in the industry's annual turnover being reduced to about 40% compared to 1920. Those with weak funds have no choice but to change their profession or close down. (3) Sales and manufacturing situation. The goods purchased by the wax industry are purchased in cash from refineries in Sichuan, Jingzhou, or Taiwen in Zhejiang, so they do not manufacture themselves. (4) Sales situation. When wax is in stock, it is sold to imperial factories and candle kilns. Before 1921, those with national savings, even if they lacked good prices, could earn about 5 yuan in pure profit for every 100 yuan of goods. Nowadays, if they want to sell goods and seek wealth, they have to lose money or exhaust their capital. (5) Comparison of the rise and fall of market prices over the years or the past year and its main reasons. During the period of stable prices, there was a slight profit when wax was sold. It is recalled that in January and February of 1921, the prices in the producing areas rose sharply. By September of that year, each clod was sold for 48 or 49 yuan. Afterwards, it plummeted to 27 or 28 yuan. In the autumn of 1923, it fell to just over 17 yuan. The highest price this year was 25 yuan, and the lowest price was 20.2 yuan, lacking buyers (each clod weighs about 57 kilograms). (6) The competition between this industry and foreign goods. The wax industry belongs to the sales industry, and except for ○○ oil, there is no competition with other industries. (7) Difficulties and relief or improvement strategies in the industry. The difficulties in the wax industry are that goods are purchased in cash, but sales are on credit, and after credit is extended, it is like there is no end in sight. Recently, foreign dealers lack the ability to digest the goods, and local soap factories and candle kilns have profited by using ○○ oil and other products, resulting in the industry not being able to make profits and losing capital. Therefore, the gross profit income is not enough to cover expenses. If relief is desired, it is useless to persuade the aforementioned factories and kilns to use domestic products. (8) The total number of employees serving in this industry and their treatment. There are nine members in the association, with about sixty-four or five employees. During the service period, in addition to the salary they should receive, there are also monthly regulations and other expenses. When dividends (bonuses) are distributed, they are determined based on the position. (9) The shops that have newly opened, reorganized, and closed down in recent years and the reasons for them. Within 1921, two shops were reorganized, and the reasons for the shops that closed down were decline and loss of capital. (10) The reports from this industry that have recently joined and not joined the association have resulted in the inability to create a report.

Literacy Education Committee: Implementing Measures for Civic Training

The content of Shanghai's literacy movement includes literacy education, common knowledge guidance, and civic training. The methods for civic training have been announced and implemented by the Literacy Education Committee. The full regulations are transcribed below:

Article 1: Civic training for students in Shanghai's public and private literacy schools and those receiving supplementary education from the Literacy Education Service Corps shall generally follow these measures.

Article 2: The content and methods of civic training are temporarily divided into the following five types: (1) New Life Movement, (2) Diligence Study Group Organization, (3) Meeting Ceremony, (4) Civic Speech, (5) Recreational Education.

Article 3: Civic training for students in public and private literacy schools shall be primarily organized by the principals and teachers of each literacy school and the district offices of each district. Civic training for those receiving supplementary education from the Literacy Education Service Corps shall be primarily organized by the leaders of each sub-group. However, district offices should also organize it as appropriate.

Article 4: The civic training organized by literacy schools should focus on the New Life Movement and Diligence Study Groups.

Article 5: The New Life Movement in literacy schools should involve the principal and teachers of the literacy school urging students to understand and implement the New Life Guidelines (emphasizing rules and cleanliness) or the Shanghai New Life Covenant, and to regularly check students' daily lives in the classroom based on the New Life Articles in Appendix 2 of these measures.

Article 6: Literacy school principals and teachers must lead by example and take the time to explain two or three items from the preceding article during each break, and write them into slogans to be posted in the classroom as a reminder.

Article 7: The organization of Diligence Study Groups for literacy school students aims to maintain school order, enhance teaching effectiveness, and promote student self-governance. It shall be carried out in accordance with the Diligence Study Group Rules in Appendix 1 of these measures.

Article 8: The civic training organized by district offices should focus on convening student fellowship gatherings. The district offices shall be responsible for directing the principals and teachers of literacy schools or the leaders of the Literacy Education Service Corps sub-groups to urge their students or those receiving supplementary education to attend (those who are unable to attend in fact may be granted leave of absence).

Article 9: The program for the fellowship gatherings in the preceding article is stipulated as follows: (1) All stand at attention, (2) Sing the Party Song (if necessary, the chairman should lead the singing, that is, the chairman sings a sentence, and the crowd echoes a sentence), (3) Bow three times to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of the Premier, (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will (must be read aloud), (5) Silence, (6) Chairman's report (if necessary, the significance of the above two to five items, i.e., the meeting ceremony, can be reported), (7) Speech (focus on materials related to political training, but strive to be clear and interesting), (8) Entertainment (including short plays, movies, primary school students singing and dancing, martial arts, skits, or gramophone records, etc., but should appropriately include educational significance, but also should not be too dull, focusing on being interesting and beneficial), (9) Adjournment (pay attention to the order when the crowd disperses).

Article 10: For the fellowship gatherings in Article 8, district offices should ensure that each student has at least one opportunity to participate each month. However, if a joint graduation ceremony is held for the second month's fellowship gathering, it may be combined with the graduation ceremony.

Article 11: The expenses for the fellowship gatherings in Article 8 shall be subsidized by the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee at a ratio of one yuan per school per event.

Article 12: The leaders of the Literacy Education Service Corps sub-groups shall organize civic training for those receiving supplementary education in accordance with the provisions of Articles 5, 6, 8, and 9 of these measures.

Article 13: The organizers of the fellowship gatherings in Articles 8 and 12 shall notify the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee three days in advance.

Article 14: These measures shall be announced and implemented by the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee and reported to the Shanghai Municipal Government for record-keeping.

Appendix 1: Shanghai Literacy Education Committee Literacy School Diligence Study Group Rules:

(1) The purpose of the Diligence Study Group is to assist literacy school teachers in maintaining school order, enhancing teaching effectiveness, and promoting student self-governance.

(2) The Diligence Study Group shall be formed by teachers assigning students from each class who live near each other. Each class may have two to five such Diligence Study Groups.

(3) The Diligence Study Group shall have one group leader, who shall be appointed by the teacher from among the members of the group who have better conduct, fewer absences, and a better spirit of service.

(4) The Diligence Study Group leader shall manage the following matters under the guidance of the teacher: 1. Supervise the members of the group to attend school on time; 2. Maintain the order of the members of the group when they arrive at school, leave school, attend class, dismiss class, and during breaks; 3. Pay attention to whether the members of the group have their literacy textbooks, supplies, or school attendance permits, and whether their clothes, hats, shoes, and pants are neat and clean; 4. Investigate and report the absences of the members of the group and the reasons for their absences.

(5) The members of the Diligence Study Group shall obey the guidance of their group leader, but the group leader shall never bully others by virtue of his position.

(6) The Diligence Study Group leader who serves diligently shall be awarded one to two pencils and notebooks per month by the school. Those who have made special contributions shall be reported to the Municipal Literacy Education Committee by the district office for reward.

(7) The Diligence Study Group leader who is negligent in his duties shall be replaced by the teacher at any time.

(8) These rules shall be announced and implemented by the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee.

Appendix 2: New Life Articles (Points to Pay Attention to in the Classroom):

(1) Sit upright, (2) Do not smoke, (3) Do not eat snacks, (4) Clothes should be simple, neat, and clean, (5) Buttons should be buttoned, (6) Shoes and pants should be worn properly, (7) Hats should be worn straight, (8) Hats should be removed when saluting, (9) Hats should be removed in assembly places, (10) Do not wear hats when entering a room, (11) Mend any tears in clothing, (12) Use domestic goods for clothing, (13) Do not go shirtless in hot weather, (14) Do not scribble on the walls, (15) Doors and windows should be kept open, (16) Rinse your mouth, wash your hair, and wash your hands often, (17) Nails should be trimmed regularly, (18) Desks and chairs should be clean, (19) Do not spit everywhere, (20) Walk on the left side of the road, (21) Do not rush when walking, (22) Do not walk too slowly, (23) If you accidentally bump into someone while walking, say "I'm sorry," (24) Enter and exit public places one by one in an orderly manner, (25) Say "Good morning" when you meet in the morning, (26) Say "Goodbye" when parting, (27) Return lost items to their owner, (28) Cherish public property, (29) Help women, children, the elderly, and the weak at any time, (30) Be focused, persistent, and sincere in doing things, (31) Do today's work today, (32) Obey class time, (33) Obey orders, accept guidance, and abide by the rules, (34) Do not flinch or shirk when encountering difficulties in doing things, (35) Always be optimistic when working, (36) Do not despise labor and laborers, (37) Pay attention to studying various new things, (38) Do not get angry easily when you are irritable, (39) Wait for others to finish speaking before speaking, (40)劝When others fight, persuade them to stop, (41) Do not curse or hit people, (42) When insulted unreasonably, reason with the person and do not endure it casually, (43) Be gentle in your tone of voice, (44) Apologize if you offend someone, (45) Respect elders, (46) Be courteous to women and children, (47) Be trustworthy to friends, (48) Listen quietly to what others say to me, (49) Do not offer cigarettes to guests, (50) Do not borrow money from others unless it is absolutely necessary.

Overseas Chinese Expelled from Japan: The 76th Batch Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Zhou Jingui and Ten Others Returned Home Aboard the Rokko Maru

The 76th batch of overseas Chinese who were forced to leave Japan, including Zhou Jingui, Chen Ruidian, Hu Wangfu, Zhu Jinying, Zhang Sanmei, Zhu Chengzhai, Liu Pinxiang (Qingtian, Zhejiang), Gao Tingji, Wang Xiuxing, and Li Jinmei (Ruian, Zhejiang), ten people in total, returned home aboard the Nippon Yusen Kaisha Rokko Maru from Tokyo, Nagoya, and other places. The situation was extremely miserable. It is planned to request relief from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau.

Ministry of Finance Corrects Tariff on Imported Small Pieces of Cloth

According to the report from the personnel sent to North China by the Municipal Machinery Dyeing and Weaving Industry Association, foreign merchants in the area were importing cotton cloth in order to avoid higher tariffs, and were cutting whole pieces into small pieces, each about one yard long (commonly known as "yard blocks"), and declaring them for import. Because the tariff rate for small pieces is less than one-third of that for whole pieces, the cost can be reduced by at least one-quarter, and even doubled for light and thin materials. Not only is sales convenient, but it is also popular with the economically backward people of North China. Domestic cloth is almost extinct under its influence. At that time, this fact was nothing more than a serious stage caused by improper tax collection procedures by the customs. The association then submitted a letter to the Ministry of Finance requesting rectification. Yesterday, the association received a reply from the Ministry of Finance stating that the customs had classified cloths less than one meter long into various whole piece tariff categories for taxation. The Customs Office No. 6599 approval is recorded as follows: "Presented, I know. Regarding the issue of taxing broken cloths cut from overseas, it has now been verified that the customs has classified cotton cloths less than one meter long into various whole piece tariff categories and taxed them according to the total number of meters imported."

According to the Central News Agency, the office and auction hall buildings under construction for the Ministry of Industry's Shanghai Fish Market can be completed this month. Liang Mengqi Returns Home After Completing His Inspection

Mr. Liang Mengqi was sent to the United States by the Guangdong authorities to inspect the chemical industry and specialize in the manufacture of various new pigments and lacquer oils. He has been inspecting in the United States for a year and has completed the inspection. He returned to China by Russian Empress ship on the 11th and arrived in Shanghai. His inspection process is recorded as follows:

Work Before Going Abroad

Mr. Liang has served as a chemical professor at National Sun Yat-sen University and Provincial Xiangqin University. He has a deep understanding of researching and applying domestic raw materials to manufacture various pigments and lacquer oils. The results of the experiments were remarkable. He has also established a factory to implement the results of his research.

Work Achievements in the United States

This time he went to the United States, he studied applied chemistry at the University of California and achieved exceptionally good results, which was highly praised by the people of the United States. He was then elected as a member by two well-known academic societies in the United States. The problem studied by Mr. Liang was to use domestic raw materials to manufacture synthetic resins commonly used in lacquer oils. The content of his paper has great value and differences and will be read at the National Congress of Chemistry in the United States. In addition to studying at the Graduate School of California, Mr. Liang traveled to various tung oil refineries, synthetic resin factories, and various lacquer oil factories in California to conduct field research. He also went to major industries in the eastern United States to inspect various chemical industries.

Job After Returning Home

Mr. Liang has now accepted an appointment as a chemistry professor at a certain university in Guangdong Province. In addition, he will continue to study the various uses of domestic tung oil, improve various old coatings, and devote himself to the production of the chemical industry, so as to benefit the people's livelihood.

Russian Car Crushes Rickshaw Driver; Deceased's Family Requests Compensation; Court Orders Driver to Post Bail

Liu Xiren from Yancheng, 26 years old, was a rickshaw driver. His family lived at No. 55 Anle Lane, Nan Shi Wai Ma Road. At noon on the 8th of this month, he was carrying a passenger and pulling car No. 1405. He was traveling from north to south in an alley next to the Grand Theater when, at that time, Russian dentist Meizha happened to be riding in his own car No. 6705. The driver, Zhang Genyang, was speeding from the east. There was no time to brake, and the rickshaw was violently overturned, and Liu was seriously injured. When the police arrived, they immediately copied down the car number and reported it to the Laozha Police Station, which summoned an ambulance. Liu was sent to Jishi Hospital for treatment but was ineffective and died soon after. After the Chinese and Western detectives went to the scene of the accident to investigate, they took the body to the Philander Road Autopsy Station. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Wei, dispatched by the First Special District District Court, went to the station and verified the body. Head Chinese Police Xue Ziwen reported the previous situation. Russian Meizha also reported that he lived on Xiafei Road in the French Concession. He said that he was sitting in the back compartment of the car that day. At that time, it happened to be raining. He saw the yellow car coming out of the alley. The driver immediately braked to avoid it to the south, but it was too late and he was hit. At that time, the driving speed was only between fifteen and seventeen yards. Zhang Gen claimed to be 51 years old, from Changshu, and had been driving a car for 20 years. The rickshaw passed through the alley that day. Because it was from high to low, it was traveling quite fast. When he saw it, he immediately braked to avoid it, but it was too late. The deceased's wife, Liu Cui, claimed that several members of her family, old and young, depended on the deceased for a living. Now that he had been killed in a car accident, she requested compensation of 5,000 yuan. The car driver claimed that the car was insured and he was unable to pay compensation. Because Mr. Guo feared that the deceased's family might need to file a private prosecution, he ordered the car driver to post bail in court so that he could be summoned when needed in the future. The car owner, Meizha, filed a case and promised to act as bail to prevent him from escaping. Mr. Guo then concluded that the deceased, Liu Xiren, male, was indeed injured and killed by car No. 6705 before his death. The body was handed over to the deceased's wife, Liu Cui, to be taken back for burial with a guarantee.

Wife's Escape Incites Fury Towards In-laws: Butcher Knife Leads to Loss of Life; Zhu Ah-san Disregards Everything, By-stander Loses Life in Vain

Local woman Xu Bu-shi, residing at No. 1297 Caojia渡, also runs the Xu He Ji butcher shop. She has two daughters. The elder daughter is married to local man Zhu Hong-kui, age thirty-nine. As Zhu is also a butcher, he helps manage the shop at Xu's place. The younger daughter once eloped, but was found by a local man named Zhu Ah-san, who returned her to her family. At the time, Zhu Ah-san was unmarried and asked someone to propose marriage to Xu, requesting her younger daughter as his wife. Xu agreed, and in October of last year, the two were married. Unexpectedly, at the beginning of this month, Zhu Xu-shi suddenly fled without a trace. Despite her husband's extensive search, she could not be found. Filled with resentment, he suspected his mother-in-law, Xu Xia-shi, of collusion, and frequently went to argue. Yesterday afternoon, he went to cause trouble again. An argument quickly escalated into a quarrel with Xu Xia-shi, even leading to physical violence. Zhu Hong-kui and Zhu Mao-di's son, who were nearby, stepped forward to mediate, seeing that Ah-san was being unreasonable. Their words inevitably offended Ah-san. Unexpectedly, Ah-san became enraged and grabbed a sharp pig-butchering knife from the meat cutting board. He indiscriminately slashed at Hong-kui, Xu Xia-shi, and Mao-di's son, all of whom were severely wounded and fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. By the time nearby patrol officers arrived, the perpetrator had already fled. They immediately reported the incident to the relevant police station for investigation and transported the injured to the hospital for treatment. However, Zhu Mao-di's son died from his severe injuries. Zhu Hong-kui suffered a knife wound to the left abdomen, with his intestines protruding, and his life is in danger. Xu Xia-shi also suffered a knife wound to the left breast, and her condition is also critical.

How Can One Bear to Take Advantage of Pleasure Seekers?: Stealing Money and Jewelry Before Departing; The Plight of the Female Tea Server is Pitiable; Shen Gen-xian Should Be Punished

Chen Cai-yun, a woman from Songjiang, is currently twenty-five years old. Six years ago, she married Chen Shun-xing, who is engaged in farming, as his wife. They were able to make a modest living from farming. In recent years, rural areas have suffered economic hardship, leading to a decline in their family's circumstances and inability to maintain their livelihood. Therefore, Chen decided to seek another way out. In January of this year, Chen came to Shanghai alone, residing at No. 8 Songgui Lane, Baxianqiao, in the French Concession. Through an introduction, she became a No. 8 female server in the Tianyun Building game hall and movie theater of the Wing On Company. After dressing up, she completely shed the image of a country girl and became a modern Chengdu woman. Due to her difficult circumstances, she inevitably engaged in some irregular activities. A nineteen-year-old man named Shen Gen-xian, whose father works as a warehouse clerk at the Yuanshun Lumber Company at No. 1105 Guangfu Road in Zhabei, also works in the lumber company as an apprentice. Shen has always been fond of women and was immediately captivated by Chen upon meeting her. He ordered tea and had a conversation with Chen, and then requested that Chen join him for an evening out. Chen agreed. They agreed on a price of ten yuan for the night. Shen paid two five-yuan bills. At 11:00 PM, they went together to the Da Zhonghua Hotel at No. 200 Xizang Road, registered under the name Wang Ke-han, and entered room 218. After spending some time together, Chen fell into a deep sleep. She had a wallet containing the ten yuan given by Shen, as well as three gold rings worth approximately eighty yuan, which she placed on the table. Unexpectedly, Shen suddenly had a bad idea. Taking advantage of Chen's deep sleep, he stole the wallet and fled. When Chen woke up at 3:30 AM, she realized that Shen and her belongings were gone. She notified the tea server Ye Bingchu. Because Chen was already married, she did not report it to the police. Unexpectedly, Shen returned to the same place at 9:00 PM on the tenth. Chen Caiyun reported him, and the No. 18 guard of the building arrested Shen and took him to the Lao Zha police station. Huatan Pang Yutang investigated. Shen initially denied it, but after being identified by Ye Bingchu and others, he could no longer deny it. Officer Pang then went to Yuanshun Lumber Company and recovered the stolen three gold rings. Yesterday morning, he escorted them to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the situation and charged him with theft under Article 321, Paragraph 1, of the Criminal Law. Because it was necessary to investigate whether the defendant had committed other similar cases, he requested a one-week adjournment. Chen Caiyun then provided evidence of the theft. Questioned by the defendant Shen Genxian, he also confessed. Judge Ye Shengchao then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing.

China Merchants Electric Company: Supplies Electricity to Songjiang and Qingpu Counties

The electricity business in Zhujiajiao in Qingpu County and Songjiang County was originally supplied separately by the Zhupu and Songjiang electric light plants. However, in recent times, the number of electricity users in these two places has gradually increased, resulting in the original power generation of the two power plants being insufficient to supply the demand. Therefore, the respective power plants requested the Shanghai China Merchants Electric Company to lay lines to supply electricity to remedy the situation. It is understood that the China Merchants Electric Company has agreed and has separately negotiated draft contracts with the respective power plants. Regarding the amount of power supply, the Zhupu plant has a maximum limit of 600 kilowatts, and the Songjiang power plant has a temporary maximum limit of 800 kilowatts. Rickshaw Pullers: Unwilling to Register, Returning to Native Places in Succession; Concerns Arise Over Fingerprinting; Vehicles are Left Idle, Cries of Hardship

The rickshaw puller registration dispute in the French Concession. Since Mr. Du Yuesheng took office to mediate, all vehicles detained by the police for not being registered have been registered free of charge and released one after another. In order to avoid misunderstandings among the rickshaw pullers, many rickshaw owners also accompanied the rickshaw pullers to register together. Therefore, as of yesterday, among the 7,100 vehicles, there were actually 1,000 rickshaw pullers registered along with the rickshaw owners. Counting one rickshaw puller per vehicle, that is not a small number. However, rickshaw pullers who have already registered are making various speculations because of the nineteen fingerprints at the time of registration. Rickshaw pullers who have not yet registered are unwilling to accept the rickshaw owners' backtracking, so they are taking boats back to their native places in Jiangbei one after another to take temporary refuge. It is said that in recent days, the passenger ships of Datong and Dada companies sailing to Tongzhou, Gaogang, and Huojiaqiao have been carrying the most of these rickshaw pullers. Although the rickshaw owners have repeatedly tried to persuade them, there are still those who secretly leave at night with their baggage. Their embarrassed situation is very pitiful. Many rickshaw companies are unable to release vehicles for morning and evening shifts due to the reduction in rickshaw pullers. For example, there are more rickshaw households in the area around Lujiabang Road, and the vehicles that are left idle have been almost full for a month. Those who make a meager profit by renting out the vehicles on behalf of others, although the contract specifies a certain number of years, have to painfully terminate the lease and are in a dilemma because there is a vehicle but no one to pull it. Those who cannot settle down are taking the path of escape. Therefore, large and small rickshaw households are all suffering from the hardship of business suspension, and the expenses of donations cannot be stopped. They are all swallowing their anger and enduring this unexpected encounter. Considering only the number of municipal license donations, in the past, at least half of the people would go to pay around the tenth of each month, but now it is said that it is less than one-tenth. The rickshaw households dare not ask the authorities to extend the old license business because the established regulations are in place and it is not convenient to change them. Therefore, this phenomenon is related to the livelihood of the poor and should be given attention by the social sector.

Public Concession: Industrial Accident Report for July

According to the工部局 report, a total of 228 accidental incidents occurred in various factories in the Public Concession in July, of which eight people died and six women were injured. The causes of the accidents, those that are generally clear, totaled 191, and those that were known after investigation totaled 109. Among the dead, there were two in the construction industry, two in the chemical industry, two in the textile industry, and one in the machinery and hardware industry.

If we classify them by type of industry, there were 53 injured in the machinery industry, 23 injured in house construction or demolition, 21 injured in the textile industry, 23 injured in the food and tobacco manufacturing industry, 20 injured in the paper and bookbinding industry, and 22 injured in the transportation industry. To discuss the causes of the disasters, there were a total of 40 injuries from machines, including one death from an elevator door injury and one death from electric shock. A total of nine people were injured in explosions, including two who died from severe injuries. A total of six people were injured in fires, including one death. A total of ten people were burned by hot objects and corrosives. Thirty-two people were injured by falling objects, including one who died from severe injuries. There were 29 injuries from falls from high places, including two deaths. There were a total of 26 injuries from impacts.

The Great China Case: Aftermath of the Settlement; The工部局 Files a Public Prosecution Again; Requesting the Court to Reopen the Debate; —The Countersuit for False Accusation Was Adjudicated Yesterday—

The fire disaster that occurred on the night of June 28 at the Xiaoshadu Road factory of the Great China Celluloid Factory. After the disaster victims and the factory were involved in litigation, Mr. Du Yuesheng and lawyer Jin Yu acted as mediators and reached a peaceful settlement outside the court last week. All lawsuits filed by both parties against each other, if in the past, the court could approve the withdrawal upon the parties' application. However, since the implementation of the new law on July 1, there are slight differences and restrictions on the application for withdrawal of the prosecution in the self-prosecution case. Therefore, the factory authorities were self-prosecuted by 40 disaster victims, and the part about public danger could not be withdrawn according to law. The court debated the case last Tuesday and scheduled it for sentencing today (13th). However, the Public Concession Police Department paid special attention to this fire and conducted a rigorous investigation afterwards. The reason why it initially did not express anything was because the investigation was still not completed. Now it has completed the investigation and decided to file a public prosecution against the person in charge of the factory on behalf of the工部局 by lawyer Ru Baoyi of the bureau's legal team. Lawyer Ru applied to the First Special District Court yesterday morning to postpone the originally scheduled sentencing period because the factory was being self-prosecuted by the victims for public danger and will be sentenced today. He said that the工部局 believed that the factory fire was related to the interests of the Public Concession, and specifically participated in the lawsuit in accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the Agreement. It should be approved to reopen the debate and reschedule the case for trial. Therefore, whether the judgment will still be announced according to the original schedule today, or the 工部局's application will be approved for re-examination, depends on the court's decision. In addition, after the disaster victims' representatives went to the factory to petition and a conflict occurred, the disaster victims self-prosecuted the chairman of the factory Zhu Rutang and Qian Menglin for injuries, and Zhu and Qian counter-sued Liu Shitong and other men and women for false accusations. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court opened the court. The police also sent many Chinese and foreign detectives to the court to assist the bailiffs in maintaining order. However, both parties did not appear in court because the case had been settled outside the court and they had applied for withdrawal of the self-prosecution. Only Gu Yongquan, the representative lawyer of Zhu and Qian, appeared. Judge Zhan declared that the case of injury filed by Liu Shitong and others had been withdrawn and the matter would not be accepted. However, the counter-prosecution for false accusations by Zhu Rutang and others could not be withdrawn according to law and should be conducted immediately. So lawyer Gu represented the two counter-prosecuting plaintiffs to state the case and asked to declare the counter-prosecuting defendants innocent. The court then announced the verdict after the conclusion of the debate. All the counter-prosecuted defendants were innocent.

The Case of Confirming an Illegitimate Child: Sent Back for Retrial After Three Lawsuits; Zhang Wubo Abandons His Wife and Children; Forensic Examination Confirms That Zhang Zhi-di Was Born to Wubo; —Both Trials Were Lost, Only the Third Trial Was Sent Back—

Zhang Wubo, a Ningbo native who runs Yongtaichang at No. 8, Taihefang, Sima Road, is 48 years old. In 1925, he met a woman named Fang Aying, who was only 14 years old at the time. Zhang seduced her because of her petite and clever nature and took her as his wife. He rented a house and cohabited with her. The following year, Fang gave birth to a son, whom Zhang named Zhimin (nickname Gougou). He loved him very much. Until 1928, Zhang suddenly made an excuse to go to Japan to do business, giving Fang 300 yuan as living expenses for her and her son. When he was about to leave, he still used the words "wait for his business to develop before holding a formal wedding" as a parting message. Therefore, Fang lived a reclusive life raising her son, but Zhang disappeared without a trace. Although she always felt the sadness of waiting for her lover, she still hoped for his return. A few years ago, she went out with her son and unexpectedly met Zhang on the way. Overjoyed to meet after a long separation, she immediately ordered her young son to call out "Father" and ask him to come home to enjoy the pleasure of family and talk about the sadness after parting.

Unexpectedly, Zhang now regarded the mother and son as strangers, turned his head and left, saying nothing. Fang was very angry and realized that his so-called going to Japan was a means of abandonment. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit against Zhang Wubo in the name of Zhimin's legal guardian to confirm the parent-child relationship. During the first trial, the defendant denied having a child with Fang. After the First Special District Court sent the child to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for examination, it was determined that he was indeed the same blood relative as the defendant and was born to the defendant. However, due to

other reasons

the First Instance Court did not consider it satisfactory, so the plaintiff's claim was rejected. Fang refused to accept it and immediately filed an appeal with the High Second Branch Court. During the court hearing, she stated that Zhang Wubo had suffered from inguinal lymphadenitis, a hidden disease that no outsider could know. This was sufficient to prove that she did live with Zhang, and the child was born during their cohabitation. There was also a forensic identification, requesting the annulment of the original judgment and confirming that Zhimin was Zhang's newly born son. However, the result of the second trial still rejected her appeal, saying that according to the provisions of the Civil Law, the right of an illegitimate child to request

paternal recognition

should be exercised within five years after the child's birth. If this right expires, it will be extinguished. Zhang Wubo is the biological father of Zhang Zhimin, but his request for recognition has passed the statutory period and should be rejected. Fang was not discouraged by the two defeats and continued to make efforts. She hired lawyer Chen Zhen to appeal to the Supreme Court, listing all the facts that she was seduced by Zhang into sexual intercourse when she was young, gave birth to a son, and then falsely claimed to go to Japan to do business and avoided seeing her. Then, after meeting on the road, he turned his eyes and acted as if he did not know her.

Betrayal

The reasons for the three points that caused her to be unable to accept the judgments of the first and second trials, and to request the annulment of the original judgment, so that all illegitimate children in the world can be spared from being fatherless children in the end. The Supreme Court recently collected the entire case file, and after a clear review, considered the second instance judgment to be particularly inappropriate and should not cite the statute of limitations for claims. Therefore, it abolished the principle and sent it to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court for retrial. Yesterday morning, the High Second Branch Court opened the court. The appellant Zhang Wubo also hired lawyer Xiong to represent him in court, while the appellants Zhang Fang, Zhang Zhimin, and mother were represented by lawyer Chen Zhen. The court briefly inquired about the facts and then announced that the hearing would be adjourned for retrial after the witnesses were summoned.

Zhang Chunfan Dies of Illness

Zhang Chunfan, the owner of the Shuliu Shanzhuang in Wujin, who became famous at home and abroad for writing novels such as Nine-tailed Turtle, served in the political circles in the north and south for many years in the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China, and was known for his integrity. In recent years, he retired to Shanghai and worked in the general management office of the Shanghai Bank to support his life. However, he suffered from paralysis of both feet last autumn, similar to a stroke. After a long period of treatment, he recovered slightly, but his health did not fully recover. On the eighth of this month, the wind disease recurred, and he suddenly passed away on the evening of the tenth. Mr. Zhang's funeral was simple, and his surviving wives and concubines had no means to support themselves. If Mr. Zhang's friends are kind enough to donate money, please send it directly to the Shanghai Bank headquarters on Ningbo Road, the Sino-Western Pharmacy headquarters on Fuzhou Road, or the Jingbao Museum on Wangping Street for delivery to Mr. Zhang's family.

Robbery on Nanjing Road in the Southern District Last Night: Police and Thieves Exchange Fire, Bullets Fly But No One is Injured

Li Xingchun, a man from Ningbo, 45 years old, has been working as a steward on Taizhou steamships. His home is located at No. 1, Qinben Lane, Wangjiazhai near Nanjing Road in the Southern District of Shanghai. Unexpectedly, at 10:30 last night, four robbers suddenly broke into his house, took out pistols, silenced the occupants, and robbed 15 silver dollars, a string of pearls, a gold bracelet, a gold bell, and two gold rings. At that time, Song Jiangshi, a neighbor of the Li family, happened to be chatting at Li Xingchun's house and was also held under surveillance by the robbers. The robbers forcibly seized two gold rings from the hands of Song Jiangshi and another neighbor, Jin Hushi, and then fled westward with the stolen goods. Liu Shaowu, the guard police officer from the 15th station, was patrolling in the area and was informed of the robbery. He immediately rushed to arrest the robbers. In a desperate situation, the robbers immediately opened fire to resist arrest. Officer Liu immediately returned fire. In an instant, gunfire erupted in Wangjiazhai, bullets flew everywhere, and passersby fled in panic. Both sides fired more than a dozen shots. Fortunately, no one was injured. The robbers, realizing the unfavorable situation due to the large number of people cooling off on the streets, did not dare to stay any longer and took the opportunity to escape into the dark alleys, disappearing without a trace. They were not apprehended. Officer Liu then returned to the police station to report the incident.

Failure in Watermelon Business Leads to Suicide by Drowning; Zhang Yu's Light Matter Costs a Life

Zhang Yuting, a native of Pudong, used to be in the fruit business. After retiring a few years ago, he opened a fruit shop in Chuansha, Pudong. However, business was slow last spring, leading to losses and the closure of the shop. He then came to Shanghai to seek employment but was unsuccessful. Zhang believed that the watermelon business in the fruit trade was booming in the summer, so he and a friend, Wang, jointly invested in the direct purchase and sale of watermelons from various production areas to Shanghai. Last autumn, after accounting, they made a considerable profit and were overjoyed. This year, after the beginning of summer, the two jointly invested in the watermelon business again, each contributing 300 silver dollars. They agreed that Zhang would be responsible for purchasing goods from farmers in the inland production areas and transporting them to Shanghai, while Wang would be responsible for selling the goods in Shanghai. However, after Zhang shipped the goods to Shanghai this summer, the market was poor. Initially, the highest price was only over two silver dollars per load, but later, with the influx of goods and poor quality, the market price plummeted, now selling for only forty or fifty cents. The weather has been rainy for days, and with the arrival of the Autumn Begins festival, sales have declined. Zhang transported watermelons to Shanghai the day before yesterday and met with Wang. After the two accounted for their finances, they found that all the capital had been lost. Zhang stated that the capital he invested was borrowed from relatives and friends at high interest, with a repayment deadline of the end of the seventh lunar month. Yesterday, Zhang told Wang that there were still four or five hundred watermelons in Tangqi that had not been shipped to Shanghai. In the morning, Zhang went to the boat of the carrier, Yang, and asked Yang to return to transport the goods. When Yang's boat sailed to the Dujiahang shore of the South Huangpu River, Zhang suddenly jumped into the river and committed suicide. The boatmen saw this, stopped the boat, and tried to rescue him for a long time, but were unsuccessful. Yang sent his assistant to Shanghai to inform Wang, who immediately rushed to Zhang's home in Chuansha to report the incident. Wang and Zhang's wife then went to the scene of the incident to retrieve the body for burial.

Shanghai North Station Ticket Supplementation Procedures for Shanghai South and West Station Passengers

The Traffic Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways yesterday announced the following regulations for supplementing tickets for passengers boarding or alighting at Shanghai North Station with tickets for Shanghai South Station and Shanghai West Station: (1) Passengers with tickets for boarding or alighting at Shanghai South Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Line may board or alight at Shanghai West Station without supplementing their tickets. (2) Passengers with tickets for boarding or alighting at Shanghai West Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Line (except for tickets between Shanghai North Station and Shanghai West Station) may board or alight at Shanghai South Station without supplementing their tickets. (3) Passengers with tickets for boarding or alighting at Shanghai West Station or Shanghai South Station who need to change to boarding or alighting at Shanghai North Station should supplement the one-way fare between Shanghai North Station and Shanghai West Station according to their class, and add a penalty according to the provisions of Announcement No. 571. The above regulations came into effect on August 11th of this year (i.e., the day before yesterday). All previous regulations have been repealed from that date.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Wang Shapa)

The Chinese people don't seem to be very interested or happy about anything else, but they are particularly fond of gambling, especially mahjong. I really can't figure out how these small 136 mahjong tiles have such a great magical power of seduction? The family of Ah Mao, the chauffeur who lives in the front building of our house, plays mahjong four weeks out of the month. The second landlord in the厢房 also has a table set up often. Even the Shandong fellows working as road construction workers in the alley, every night, have to go to the tiger stove across the street to play a few "铲" five hundred "铲". Many women would rather put aside their housework and play eight or twelve rounds. Some people even find it not enjoyable enough to gamble at home, and they even rent hotels to gamble big, as if they can eat less, but they can't stop playing mahjong? In fact, playing mahjong is the most uneconomical thing. Thinking about it, it's really a little tasteless. When four people sit down to gamble, there are winners and losers. However, losing money is still a small matter. The loss of spirit and the waste of time are probably greater than losing money.

Model Women's Prison

— Hua Ling

A friend who returned from studying in France told me, "In the French province of Fresnes, there is a women's prison. Serving time in this prison is more comfortable than living at home."

He said, "This prison is like a villa. The squares and flower beds are arranged into a large square garden.

"In this prison, children are allowed to stay with their mothers. According to their regulations, mothers are not allowed to abandon their children if they commit crimes. At the very least, they must stay with their children until they are four years old before being separated. However, in reality, mothers and children are often inseparable, and they are released together after the mother's sentence expires.

"The prison buildings are similar to other prisons, with iron bars for security. However, these frightening iron bars are painted in pleasant colors. The lighting at night is also very good. Each prisoner's room has a large bed and a small bed or a cradle. Everything is similar to living in a dormitory, except that they do not have the freedom to leave. However, their children can play outside in the yard all day long.

"The prison guards in this prison do not treat the female prisoners with children with harsh expressions, to prevent the children from having a bad impression that will be forever imprinted on their minds.

"Therefore, women who are released from that prison after serving their sentences often become good people because they have been influenced for the better."

It is said that in France, this prison is called the "French Model Women's Prison," and they are preparing to implement this prison system nationwide.

Poetry Riddles

— Rong Yu

Poetry riddles, also known as "poetry treasures," involve taking a line from a five- or seven-character poem, or an ancient-style poem, removing one character, and adding four identical characters next to the line, allowing people to guess. The winner receives triple the bet. This is truly a game of gambling with poetry. During the Qing Dynasty, during the annual civil service examinations, idle scholars would set up stalls next to the examination hall, luring candidates to participate. Although these candidates had some literary knowledge and could recite a few examination poems, they found it difficult to figure out good riddles and usually lost nine out of ten times, leaving them with empty pockets. As for poetry riddles in Shanghai, they first appeared next to the grain depot behind the City God Temple, occasionally set up outdoors during the New Year, with the participants being mostly peddlers and laborers. Even though they were illiterate, they found it interesting to guess based on the "treasure path." Around 1922-1923, someone started setting up stalls in the New World Amusement Park, offering white tin-foiled "Craven A" cigarettes as prizes. As a result, men and women with little literacy pretended to be poets, pondering and guessing. The business flourished, and one stall turned into more than ten. Subsequently, the Great World and other amusement parks also followed suit. Various associations and street corners also had poetry riddles set up, creating a surging trend that surpassed even the stock market frenzy of that year. It is feared that many people were ruined and driven to suicide as a result. After this trend lasted for two or three years, people got tired of it, and the authorities cracked down on it. As a result, the "poetry masters" disappeared, and the riddle strips were put away. Currently, only the Guan Yun Poetry Collection on Avenue Edward VII remains, but the business is not thriving.

Poetry riddles originated from ancient hidden language and cryptic words, similar to "shooting covers." The best riddle strips are balanced in five characters, seamless, and truly make the guessers feel confused and difficult to grasp. Some deliberately use awkward sentences and vulgar words, which is like using unorthodox tactics in warfare. It may work once in a while, but using it too much will not be effective. Later, cunning people used plum blossom scripts to create the strips, which was no different from cheating in Pai Gow. As a result, scholars stayed away, and the "riddle fortune" came to an end.

All Men Share the Same Heart, Hearts Share the Same Reason.

— Juan Yin

Kissing

— Jian Wen

Is kissing a kind of epidemic? Physiologists should admit that it is. Just imagine, when lips touch lips, isn't it easy to transmit germs?

However, from another perspective, the lips are tactile organs, with extremely sensitive feelings, and are an important tool for human expression. Smiling, containing anger, pursing lips, anger... can all be revealed through the movement of the lips. Movie actors pay great attention to these changes in lip movements. Because kissing is a behavior that excites emotions and expresses affection.

For this reason, young people and middle-aged people like to kiss children, which is certainly not objectionable; young people and young people, middle-aged people and middle-aged people, men and women kissing each other, we have no reason to criticize. But why is kissing considered a secret that cannot be made public in Chinese society?

It is said that when French soldiers receive medals, the officers kiss the soldiers on both cheeks as a solemn ceremony. This shows that kissing can be regarded as a different kind of perversion in societies that do not have this custom, and is considered a secret and shameful thing.

In the future, for the sake of health and hygiene, we should not arbitrarily kiss innocent children; for the sake of respecting people's freedom of expression, we should not take the kissing between middle-aged and young people too seriously!

Local Customs

Japanese Cleanliness Campaign

— Ji Yun

Foreigners who have been to China always say that China is unclean and unhygienic. Since the New Life Movement has been carried out in various places, the public may gradually pay attention to it. Now I will present the Japanese cleanliness campaign to the readers as a reference.

Japanese houses are all made of wood and are not painted, so they are theoretically easy to get dirty. However, they all have straw mats inside, filled with rice husks underneath. Walking on them with indoor socks is very soft. Every morning after getting up, the housewife sprinkles wet tea leaves on the mats, wears a mask, and sweeps the room. Then, she wipes the windows and railings with a damp cloth. The outdoor floor is also wiped with a damp cloth. Holding the rag with both hands, she bends forward and pushes forward, which we call "driving a streetcar." The handrails in the stairwell and the toilets must also be washed by hand. Very few Japanese families hire maids, and most of them are done by the housewives themselves.

Each household has a wooden trash can at the door, with the words "For the exclusive use of so-and-so" written on it. Every morning, the street cleaners shake a bell and come to sweep. The streets or sidewalks outside the door are swept two or three times a day, sometimes with a long-handled palm brush. They like to sprinkle water on the road to prevent dust. Fortunately, they all wear leather shoes and clogs, which does not interfere with this. In China, it may be annoying to pedestrians.

Taking a bath for five cents is a daily routine for Japanese people. They wash their bodies clean before soaking in the bath, so the water in the pool is always very clear. Ordinary bathwater contains carbolic acid, and those along the coast use seawater. They shave themselves and shave their sons' heads in the bathhouse without spending a penny.

Of course, there are also flies. Once, in a public cemetery, I saw thousands of flies on the tombstones. I don't know why. They usually keep many pieces of white paper in their pockets to wipe their noses. But there are no fewer people spitting everywhere than in our country, but it is not common indoors. Also, laborers often urinate at will by the ditches in the small alleys. Even in Japan, which is famous for its cleanliness, this bad habit is still difficult to completely correct. If our country can pay attention to it, it may not be inferior to them.

The Japanese police do a good job. They don't often stay in the station, but often carry household registration books to check everywhere. So how many people are in each household and how they act cannot escape their eyes and ears. Restaurants and hotels are inspected very strictly, and kitchens and toilets must be inspected. As long as there is no stinky disinfectant in the spittoon, there is a risk of punishment. General cleaning is held several times a year, approximately on a certain date. During the cleaning, the heavy objects in the house are moved to the sidewalk for a thorough cleaning.

Around six or seven in the morning, all the shop assistants are mobilized to clean, and the counters and display windows are spotless. The glass doors along the street are wiped once or twice a day. The things used in the barbershop are usually soaked in disinfectant, and only taken out when they are used. The beard and soap foam shaved off are wiped on white paper and not thrown away. Barbers, regardless of gender, wear masks to protect their mouths from the heat, which may disgust customers.

The excrement is handled by the city government, which hires workers to dump the excrement from people's homes. It is also loaded with buckets, which are tightly covered and will never spill out, and there is not much odor. More than a dozen manure buckets are loaded on a two-wheeled truck, covered with oilcloth, and carried by hand to the warehouse. The time for dumping manure seems to be in the morning and afternoon, but there is no specific time.

Little Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 17: Do Not Ask About a Daughter's Gender, Difficult to Express Hidden Pain, Competing to See the Face of a Distinguished Person, Admiring Lofty Character Together

Zhiqian continued: If it's about helping a little, I can't say I can't do it. How about this, I'll give you some money so you can buy some snacks on the road. Saying this, he took out a five-yuan bill from his pocket and placed it on the table in front of Wanhua. Wanhua couldn't help but show a smile on her face. Holding onto the table, she stood up and said: Thank you, thank you! I have no other choice. Saying this, she lowered her head to look at the bill. Zhiqian said: Just take it, I took it out, of course, I don't mean it falsely. If you think it's too little... Wanhua shook her head and said: I would never dare. Only then did she slowly put the bill into her pocket. As if there was something else, not very comfortable, she sat down again, forcing a smile and saying: I'm really embarrassed, I have no relationship with Mr. Cheng, but I'm costing Mr. Cheng. Zhiqian smiled: Only because I'm in a detached position, I can help a little. Otherwise, why would I take out this money, that would be too difficult. Wanhua sat down again, lowering her head. Zhiqian was afraid that she would have some other requests, so he lit a cigarette for guests and smoked it very boredly. Wanhua slowly raised her head and asked: Mr. Cheng will probably have to stay in Xi'an for some time, right? Zhiqian said: That's not certain. Wanhua tidied her hair, smiled and said: Your wife must miss you very much at home. Zhiqian said: I'm always out and about, so it doesn't matter. Wanhua lowered her head, raised her hands, and slowly flipped them over to look, asking: Will Mr. Cheng have guests coming tonight? Zhiqian said sternly: Miss Yang, I've already said, I'm purely helping you a little, you don't need to think too much. I should go out to see friends. (288)

Records of Piao Miao Royal Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

At this time, the eyes of all the people were already firmly fixed on that green carpet-like lotus grove; I myself was especially excited, my two eyes desperately enlarged, enlarging and enlarging again—just like those plump buds were enlarging at the same time. Indeed, they were enlarging there too! Hundreds, thousands of them, wherever our sight could reach, all had their shadows, none of them were not enlarging, shaking, and releasing.

The sun rose higher and higher, already half hung up.

Those thousands of hundreds of buds were also opening bigger and bigger.

As the sun rose completely and the lotus flowers bloomed completely, a fresh, fragrant smell was added to the air, blowing over our heads, stroking our sides, and it seemed that people's breaths were also fragrant. This is the most lovely lotus fragrance! At that time, half of the eastern rosy clouds had covered half of the sky, and were about to invade the west. Those lotus buds attracted the attention of every spectator, and everyone felt that this was the most lovely scene, each bud was like a child's small fist, and those petals were even more like plump, white, and tender little fingers; when they opened, it was exactly like a child waking up and slowly unfolding his little fist, which was indeed worthy of appreciation.

Because I had just heard the Empress Dowager say that we should "listen", so I pricked up my ears and listened attentively; in reality, I couldn't hear any sound at all, only because I was influenced by psychological effects; I seemed to really have heard the rustling sound of those lotus flowers opening (388)

Page 13
